Calibration and Sensitivity: The sensor is calibrated using standard solutions of quinine at known concentrations. The electrochemical response (such as current or potential change) is measured as quinine displaces a pre-bound indicator from a host molecule on the sensor surface. A calibration curve is constructed to determine the sensor's sensitivity and linear range.\n\n2. Selectivity: The sensor's response to quinine is compared to its response to structurally similar compounds or potential interferents (e.g., other alkaloids, ions, or common pharmaceuticals) to ensure that the IDA mechanism is selective for quinine.\n\n3. Limit of Detection (LOD) and Limit of Quantification (LOQ): The lowest concentration of quinine that can be reliably detected and quantified is determined, often using statistical analysis of the signal-to-noise ratio.\n\n4. Calibration and Sensitivity: The sensor is calibrated using standard solutions of quinine at known concentrations. The electrochemical response (such as current or potential change) is measured as quinine displaces a pre-bound indicator from a host molecule on the sensor surface. A calibration curve is constructed to determine the sensor's sensitivity and linear range.\n\n2. Selectivity: The sensor's response to quinine is compared to its response to structurally similar compounds or potential interferents (e.g., other alkaloids, ions, or common pharmaceuticals) to ensure that the IDA mechanism is selective for quinine.\n\n3. Limit of Detection (LOD) and Limit of Quantification (LOQ): The lowest concentration of quinine that can be reliably detected and quantified is determined, often using statistical analysis of the signal-to-noise ratio.\n\n4. Reproducibility and Stability: The sensor's performance is tested over multiple measurements and over time to assess reproducibility and operational stability.\n\n5. Recovery and Real Sample Analysis: The sensor is tested in real or spiked samples (such as beverages or biological fluids) to evaluate its practical applicability and recovery rate for quinine.\n\n6.
